<div id="review_676995659" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/676995659" />
    <a title="Ric" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2990467-ric"><img alt="Ric" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514254938p2/2990467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/676995659?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ric" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ric" href="/user/show/2990467-ric">Ric</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/13345121-the-end-of-eternity">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer676995659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5194719482358958723">Re-read of an SF Classic. <br/><br/>There are numerous time travel stories in the literature, including <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/778990.Timescape' title='Timescape by Gregory Benford' rel='nofollow noopener'>Timescape</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22645.Gregory_Benford' title='Gregory Benford' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gregory Benford</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27833670.Dark_Matter' title='Dark Matter by Blake Crouch' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dark Matter</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/442240.Blake_Crouch' title='Blake Crouch' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blake Crouch</a> with their multiplying timelines, but this early entry by the master <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov' title='Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Isaac Asimov</a>, is one of the leading examples of the immutable timeline. In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/509784.The_End_of_Eternity' title='The End of Eternity by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>The End of Eternity</a>, mankind has discovered the secret of time travel, and in the process further determined that there is only one reality or timeline, which can be changed to a large or small degree </span>
  <span id="freeText5194719482358958723" style="display:none">Re-read of an SF Classic. <br /><br />There are numerous time travel stories in the literature, including <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/778990.Timescape" title="Timescape by Gregory Benford" rel="nofollow noopener">Timescape</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22645.Gregory_Benford" title="Gregory Benford" rel="nofollow noopener">Gregory Benford</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27833670.Dark_Matter" title="Dark Matter by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Matter</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/442240.Blake_Crouch" title="Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Blake Crouch</a> with their multiplying timelines, but this early entry by the master <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Isaac Asimov</a>, is one of the leading examples of the immutable timeline. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/509784.The_End_of_Eternity" title="The End of Eternity by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">The End of Eternity</a>, mankind has discovered the secret of time travel, and in the process further determined that there is only one reality or timeline, which can be changed to a large or small degree by time travelers fiddling with historical events. So is born the controlling organization known as Eternity, formed to ensure that mankind's future is secured by eliminating all events that could lead to his extinction. But is Eternity truly serving mankind with its charter, or by acting as ultimate arbiter of history, in fact, is behaving like a dictatorial overlord of the race?<br /><br />To my mind, Asimov embodied the essential nature of SF, which is the optimistic belief that man will solve all his problems and challenges with science, and, in this way, control his destiny. Elements of this can be found in the psychohistory of his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29579.Foundation__Foundation__1_" title="Foundation (Foundation #1) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation</a> books by which man is able to predict his future century by mathematically modelling the historical and present human society and extrapolating forward. Asimov also pioneered the idea that with the same evolutionary path, the emergent species would be humanoid, not that much different from humans of Earth, even without any interchange of data or seed. Hence, we are not out-liers but are the normative life form of this universe. A truly positive viewpoint, polar opposite to the dystopia that has recently prevailed in contemporary SF.<br /><br />This was a fun re-read, bringing back many memories of my youth, and positive ones certainly. This reminded me of why I read SF, and why it has played a major role in my outlook and world view. Maybe science cannot solve everything, and I know by experience it cannot, but it can set the platform for working things out and focusing on the issues. <br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5194719482358958723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_392323819" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/392323819" />
    <a title="Tej" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5798859-tej"><img alt="Tej" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315232929p2/5798859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/392323819?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tej" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tej" href="/user/show/5798859-tej">Tej</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5798859-tej?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392323819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4788661620755791803">This is vintage Asimov, a novel exuding brilliance in imagination and intelligent philosophising of possible future realities. How better to muse about what different realities we can face about the future from near to far to...eternity, without the plot device of time travelling. Asimov puts this plot device to great use by exploring the various destinies that human motives can achieve or fall victim of. The story ingeniously threads these philosophical questions and tells a story about eternit</span>
  <span id="freeText4788661620755791803" style="display:none">This is vintage Asimov, a novel exuding brilliance in imagination and intelligent philosophising of possible future realities. How better to muse about what different realities we can face about the future from near to far to...eternity, without the plot device of time travelling. Asimov puts this plot device to great use by exploring the various destinies that human motives can achieve or fall victim of. The story ingeniously threads these philosophical questions and tells a story about eternity through another more common and oldest of plot devices, a love story. <br /><br />The only problem with the story is that the main protagonist, Harlan, is an unlikeable, pitiful and naive character. But there is reward to bare up with him as these attributes are essential to serving the story. We follow his journey as he is recruited through the ranks as an Eternal, a technician serving to make changes in time for reasons I leave for you to discover in the novel.<br /><br />He is dedicated to his work until he meets a non Eternal woman and falls in love with her. One could interpret as love, lust or even be victim to a love enchantment by the woman, regardless, the effect his feelings for her have on him changes his perspective of his surrounding to that of dangerous paranoia or apparent clarity. And its from here that the author toys with our own perspectives on where this story is going, swinging the pendulum left to right until I became dazed with all the sharp corner turns.<br /><br />Bizarrely, given the scope of the premise, the narrative is quite claustrophobic but this gives the story a tighter hold. The Journey entails several enjoyable moments of time travel concepts, such as the effects of meeting one's younger self and other time travel cause and effect events. Its highly entertaining.<br /><br />This is actually quite a short read, perhaps mercifully so as I am not sure I could handle more techno-babble on the Eternals structure and I think I would throw up if the car turned one more sharp corner. So the length is just right, just took a little patience to bare up with the slow and overly technical exposition and Harlan's naivety before the novel grabbed me by the scruff of the neck and whisked me through a twisty philosophical ride in Eternity.<br /><br />4.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4788661620755791803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2395533790" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2395533790" />
    <a title="Manuel Alfonseca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35970992-manuel-alfonseca"><img alt="Manuel Alfonseca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420279369p2/35970992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2395533790?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manuel Alfonseca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manuel Alfonseca" href="/user/show/35970992-manuel-alfonseca">Manuel Alfonseca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2395533790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16333113214479593007">ENGLISH: This book is quite similar to "Guardians of time" by Poul Anderson, but in a certain sense it is also its opposite. In both cases, time travel is supposed to be possible and the present can be changed by manipulating the past. But in Anderson's series of stories, our far descendants stage the time guardians to prevent those changes in the past that would affect their own existence. What happens in Asimov's novel is quite the opposite. This is understandable, for the end of the novel mak</span>
  <span id="freeText16333113214479593007" style="display:none">ENGLISH: This book is quite similar to "Guardians of time" by Poul Anderson, but in a certain sense it is also its opposite. In both cases, time travel is supposed to be possible and the present can be changed by manipulating the past. But in Anderson's series of stories, our far descendants stage the time guardians to prevent those changes in the past that would affect their own existence. What happens in Asimov's novel is quite the opposite. This is understandable, for the end of the novel makes possible the plot of the Foundation trilogy.<br /><br />In any case, the novel is atypical, for this type of time travel usually has a component of alternative history, which in Asimov's novel is glaringly absent.<br /><br />ESPAÑOL: Este libro es bastante similar a "La Patrulla del Tiempo" de Poul Anderson, pero en cierto sentido es exactamente opuesta. En ambos casos, se supone que los viajes en el tiempo son posibles y que el presente puede cambiarse manipulando el pasado. Pero en la serie de historias de Anderson, nuestros lejanos descendientes montan la patrulla del tiempo para evitar que los cambios en el pasado afecten su propia existencia. Lo que sucede en la novela de Asimov es todo lo contrario. Esto es comprensible, porque el final de la novela enlaza con la trama de la trilogía de la Fundación.<br /><br />En cualquier caso, la novela es atípica, ya que este tipo de viajes en el tiempo suele tener un componente de historia alternativa, que en la novela de Asimov está totalmente ausente.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16333113214479593007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3107051021" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3107051021" />
    <a title="Bon Tom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40807670-bon-tom"><img alt="Bon Tom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511016606p2/40807670.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3107051021?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bon Tom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bon Tom" href="/user/show/40807670-bon-tom">Bon Tom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40807670-bon-tom?shelf=normal-sized">normal-sized</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40807670-bon-tom?shelf=masterpiece">masterpiece</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40807670-bon-tom?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40807670-bon-tom?shelf=sf">sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3107051021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6493499287790193756">There comes a day when you have to let your kid walk alone and do the trip to school by himself. You tell him to watch the traffic, and hope for the best, e.e. that he'll get back in one piece.<br/><br/>That's how I felt when I just decided to let my brain take the trip of this book, although I won't be following him every step of the way. Because I just couldn't. But I knew it would be good for him.<br/><br/>It came back changed. He was telling me about what he experienced along the way. I was listening with aston</span>
  <span id="freeText6493499287790193756" style="display:none">There comes a day when you have to let your kid walk alone and do the trip to school by himself. You tell him to watch the traffic, and hope for the best, e.e. that he'll get back in one piece.<br /><br />That's how I felt when I just decided to let my brain take the trip of this book, although I won't be following him every step of the way. Because I just couldn't. But I knew it would be good for him.<br /><br />It came back changed. He was telling me about what he experienced along the way. I was listening with astonishment, without a trace of fainted interest, but still I didn't completely get it.<br /><br />This SF is as hard boiled as it gets. Books that deal with time travel always are. You need to cling to the last atoms of your attention in order not to lose the cosmic string of matrix that holds it all together.<br /><br />I lost it pretty early on. I ended up imagining I was 50.000 year old man going on 25, when, in reality, it was only 1936, still decades from my birth. Still, newspapers were full of interesting news, my toast hot and butter just right, so I decided to play along.<br /><br />Paperboy on the street was yelling Extra! Extra!<br /><br />My brain pretends and tries to convince me he didn't experience anything unusual.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6493499287790193756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_27305093" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27305093" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1019174-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555890512p2/1019174.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27305093?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/1019174-terence">Terence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780739435571" href="/book/show/144530.The_End_of_Eternity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019174-terence?shelf=sf-fantasy">sf-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27305093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9317939571950721283">I don't know whether I began reading Asimov's nonfiction or fiction works first. I <i>do</i> know that I wrote a fan letter to him and actually got a reply back. Granted, it was a form-letter postcard but it was still pretty "cool" that I was "corresponding" with an actual author.<br/><br/>I was also very selective in what I read. I enjoyed the first three books of the <i>Foundation</i> but I never had any desire to read any of the <i>Robot</i> novels, and subsequent <i>Foundation</i> novels were disappointing (with the brilliant ex</span>
  <span id="freeText9317939571950721283" style="display:none">I don't know whether I began reading Asimov's nonfiction or fiction works first. I <i>do</i> know that I wrote a fan letter to him and actually got a reply back. Granted, it was a form-letter postcard but it was still pretty "cool" that I was "corresponding" with an actual author.<br /><br />I was also very selective in what I read. I enjoyed the first three books of the <i>Foundation</i> but I never had any desire to read any of the <i>Robot</i> novels, and subsequent <i>Foundation</i> novels were disappointing (with the brilliant exception of Kingsbury's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1518819.Psychohistorical_Crisis" title="Psychohistorical Crisis by Donald Kingsbury" rel="nofollow noopener">Psychohistorical Crisis</a>, I stopped after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29582.Foundation_and_Earth__Foundation__5_" title="Foundation and Earth (Foundation #5) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation and Earth</a>). "Nightfall" is one of my favorite short stories but off the top of my head I can't remember any other Asimov short that I've read. Even at the age of thirteen (or so), I recognized something lacking; he was a competent enough writer and the hard SF ideas he played with were interesting but the writing itself often lacked that "certain something" that made me want to read more.<br /><br /><i>The End of Eternity</i> is in that category. I've had a hankering to reread it for the last few months. When I saw a copy on my library's shelf, I grabbed it. It rates a 2.5 on the GR scale because it raises some interesting notions about time travel and the idea that only by risking great suffering and catastrophic failure can a person or a species achieve great success. A notion that has informed my own view of the world, and whose origins, to some extent, can doubtless be traced back to reading this book. Elsewise, characters and plot are subordinated to the "idea" of Eternity and its deleterious effects on humanity.<br /><br />As an aside, Mark Rosenfelder's Zompist.com webpage has a marvelous dissection of the entire <i>Foundation</i> series, both Asimov's sequels and the other volumes written by Bear, Brin &amp; Kingsbury <a href="http://www.zompist.com/asimov.htm" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9317939571950721283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HjL6ycDhy0XtmAz5Wt9TpTMd2tqTNDwWTG0ZJAoDpT8kFJMbe78CLUqzuJitKll65UI9El25snEXE1+Vx0BXpQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HSkxM9//x2l1f6KGkxoXx6esC//WT4cxUtOhpOydMzMnD1jhZKEOAdJUFudk7x0YcfPsNxjCCVYJrecVId7BqQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov">About Isaac Asimov</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1341965730p3/16667.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov">Isaac Asimov
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
19,205
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8133021820209912767">Isaac Asimov was a Russian-born, American author, a professor of biochemistry, and a highly successful writer, best known for his works of science fiction and for his popular science books.<br/><br/>Professor Asimov is generally considered one of the most prolific writers of all time, having written or edited more than 500 books and an estimated 90,000 letters and postcards. He has works published in nine o</span>
  <span id="freeText8133021820209912767" style="display:none">Isaac Asimov was a Russian-born, American author, a professor of biochemistry, and a highly successful writer, best known for his works of science fiction and for his popular science books.<br /><br />Professor Asimov is generally considered one of the most prolific writers of all time, having written or edited more than 500 books and an estimated 90,000 letters and postcards. He has works published in nine of the ten major categories of the Dewey Decimal System (lacking only an entry in the 100s category of Philosophy).<br /><br />Asimov is widely considered a master of the science-fiction genre and, along with Robert A. Heinlein and Arthur C. Clarke, was considered one of the "Big Three" science-fiction writers during his lifetime. Asimov's most famous work is the Foundation Series; his other major series are the Galactic Empire series and the Robot series, both of which he later tied into the same fictional universe as the Foundation Series to create a unified "future history" for his stories much like those pioneered by Robert A. Heinlein and previously produced by Cordwainer Smith and Poul Anderson. He penned numerous short stories, among them "Nightfall", which in 1964 was voted by the Science Fiction Writers of America the best short science fiction story of all time, a title many still honor. He also wrote mysteries and fantasy, as well as a great amount of nonfiction. Asimov wrote the Lucky Starr series of juvenile science-fiction novels using the pen name Paul French.<br /><br />Most of Asimov's popularized science books explain scientific concepts in a historical way, going as far back as possible to a time when the science in question was at its simplest stage. He often provides nationalities, birth dates, and death dates for the scientists he mentions, as well as etymologies and pronunciation guides for technical terms. Examples include his Guide to Science, the three volume set Understanding Physics, and Asimov's Chronology of Science and Discovery.<br /><br />Asimov was a long-time member and Vice President of Mensa International, albeit reluctantly; he described some members of that organization as "brain-proud and aggressive about their IQs" He took more joy in being president of the American Humanist Association. The asteroid 5020 Asimov, the magazine Asimov's Science Fiction, a Brooklyn, NY elementary school, and two different Isaac Asimov Awards are named in his honor.<br /><br />----------------------------------------<br /><i>Isaac Asimov. (2007, November 29). In Wikipedia, The Free Encyclopedia. Retrieved 21:50, November 29, 2007, from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Asimov">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_As...</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8133021820209912767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
